<table class="infobox nowrap" style="width:22em"><caption style="white-space:normal; padding-bottom:0.15em;">Sugar (sucrose), granulated</caption><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Nutritional value per 100&#160;g (3.5&#160;oz)</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Food_energy" title="Food energy">Energy</a></th><td>1,619&#160;kJ (387&#160;kcal)</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><div style="position:relative;left:-0.65em;"><b><a href="/wiki/Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate">Carbohydrates</a></b></div></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><div style="position:relative;left:-0.65em;">99.98 g</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Sugars</a></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;">99.91 g</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><a href="/wiki/Dietary_fiber" title="Dietary fiber">Dietary fiber</a></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;">0 g</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><div style="position:relative;left:-0.65em;"><b><a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">Fat</a></b></div></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><div style="position:relative;left:-0.65em;">0 g</div></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><div style="position:relative;left:-0.65em;"><b><a href="/wiki/Protein_(nutrient)" title="Protein (nutrient)">Protein</a></b></div></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><div style="position:relative;left:-0.65em;">0 g</div></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><b style="margin-left:-0.65em"><a href="/wiki/Vitamin" title="Vitamin">Vitamins</a></b></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><b>Quantity</b> <span style="float:right;"><abbr title="Percentage of Daily Value"><b>%DV</b></abbr><sup>†</sup></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><a href="/wiki/Riboflavin" title="Riboflavin">Riboflavin <span style="font-size:90%;">(B<span style="position: relative; top: 0.35em;"><span style="font-size:90%;">2</span></span>)</span></a></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><div style="float: right;">2%</div> 0.019 mg</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><b style="margin-left:-0.65em"><a href="/wiki/Mineral_(nutrient)" title="Mineral (nutrient)">Minerals</a></b></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><b>Quantity</b> <span style="float:right;"><abbr title="Percentage of Daily Value"><b>%DV</b></abbr><sup>†</sup></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><a href="/wiki/Calcium_in_biology#Humans" title="Calcium in biology">Calcium</a></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><div style="float: right;">0%</div> 1 mg</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><a href="/wiki/Human_iron_metabolism" title="Human iron metabolism">Iron</a></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><div style="float: right;">0%</div> 0.01 mg</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><a href="/wiki/Potassium_in_biology" title="Potassium in biology">Potassium</a></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><div style="float: right;">0%</div> 2 mg</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;"><b style="margin-left:-0.65em">Other constituents</b></th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;"><b>Quantity</b></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;">Water</th><td style="vertical-align:middle;padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;">0.03 g</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><hr /><div class="wrap" style="font-size:90%;padding:0.3em;line-height:1.2em;"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ndb.nal.usda.gov/ndb/foods/show/6319">Full link to USDA database entry</a></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div class="plainlist" style="font-size:90%;background:#e0e0e0;padding:0.15em;line-height:1.25em;">
<ul><li>Units</li>
<li>μg = <a href="/wiki/Microgram" title="Microgram">micrograms</a>&#160;&#8226;&#32;mg = <a href="/wiki/Milligram" class="mw-redirect" title="Milligram">milligrams</a></li>
<li>IU = <a href="/wiki/International_unit" title="International unit">International units</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="wrap" style="text-align:center;font-size:90%;background:#e0e0e0;padding:0.3em;line-height:1.5em;font-weight:normal;"><sup>†</sup>Percentages are roughly approximated using <a href="/wiki/Dietary_Reference_Intake" title="Dietary Reference Intake">US&#160;recommendations</a> for adults.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Brown and white granulated sugar are 97% to nearly 100% <a href="/wiki/Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate">carbohydrates</a>, respectively, with less than 2% water, and no dietary fiber, protein or fat (table). Brown sugar contains a moderate amount of iron (15% of the <a href="/wiki/Reference_Daily_Intake" title="Reference Daily Intake">Reference Daily Intake</a> in a 100 gram amount, see table), but a typical serving of 4 grams (one teaspoon), would provide 15 <a href="/wiki/Calorie" title="Calorie">calories</a> and a negligible amount of iron or any other nutrient.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Because brown sugar contains 5–10% <a href="/wiki/Molasses" title="Molasses">molasses</a> reintroduced during processing, its value to some consumers is a richer flavor than white sugar.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_effects">Health effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Health effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sugar_industry_funding_and_health_information">Sugar industry funding and health information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sugar industry funding and health information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sugar_marketing#Influence_on_health_information_and_guidelines" title="Sugar marketing">Sugar marketing §&#160;Influence on health information and guidelines</a></div>
<p>Sugar refiners and manufacturers of sugary foods and drinks have sought to influence medical research and <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> recommendations,<sup id="cite_ref-conflict_2017_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conflict_2017-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sweet_policies_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sweet_policies-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> with substantial and largely clandestine spending documented from the 1960s to 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-jama2016_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jama2016-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kearns_caries_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kearns_caries-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-selling_souls_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-selling_souls-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sponsorship_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sponsorship-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The results of research on the health effects of sugary food and drink differ significantly, depending on whether the researcher has financial ties to the food and drink industry.<sup id="cite_ref-Schillinger_bias_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schillinger_bias-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-financial_Bes-Rasttrollo_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financial_Bes-Rasttrollo-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT_linked_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_linked-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> A 2013 medical review concluded that "unhealthy commodity industries should have no role in the formation of national or international NCD [<a href="/wiki/Non-communicable_disease" title="Non-communicable disease">non-communicable disease</a>] policy".<sup id="cite_ref-profits_pandemics_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profits_pandemics-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There have been similar efforts to steer coverage of sugar-related health information in popular media, including news media and social media.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_cocacola_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_cocacola-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT_sweettalk_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_sweettalk-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-time_soda_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time_soda-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Obesity_and_metabolic_syndrome">Obesity and metabolic syndrome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Obesity and metabolic syndrome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 2003 <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> technical report provided evidence that high intake of sugary drinks (including <a href="/wiki/Fruit_juice" class="mw-redirect" title="Fruit juice">fruit juice</a>) increased the risk of <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a> by adding to overall <a href="/wiki/Energy_intake" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy intake">energy intake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO2003_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2003-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> By itself, sugar is not a factor causing obesity and <a href="/wiki/Metabolic_syndrome" title="Metabolic syndrome">metabolic syndrome</a>, but rather – when over-consumed – is a component of unhealthy dietary behavior.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO2003_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2003-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Meta-analysis" title="Meta-analysis">Meta-analyses</a> showed that excessive consumption of sugar-sweetened beverages increased the risk of developing <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_type_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Diabetes mellitus type 2">type 2 diabetes</a> and metabolic syndrome – including weight gain and obesity – in adults and children.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Addiction">Addiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Addiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 2018 <a href="/wiki/Systematic_review" title="Systematic review">systematic review</a> concluded that the potential for <a href="/wiki/Sugar_addiction" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar addiction">sugar addiction</a> was greater when in combination with dietary <a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">fats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid29649120_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid29649120-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hyperactivity">Hyperactivity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Hyperactivity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 2019 <a href="/wiki/Meta-analysis" title="Meta-analysis">meta-analysis</a> found that sugar consumption does not improve <a href="/wiki/Mood_(psychology)" title="Mood (psychology)">mood</a>, but can lower alertness and increase fatigue within an hour of consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Some studies report evidence of <a href="/wiki/Causality" title="Causality">causality</a> between high consumption of refined sugar and <a href="/wiki/Hyperactivity" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperactivity">hyperactivity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> One review of low-quality studies of children consuming high amounts of <a href="/wiki/Energy_drink" title="Energy drink">energy drinks</a> showed association with higher rates of unhealthy behaviors, including smoking and alcohol abuse, and with hyperactivity and <a href="/wiki/Insomnia" title="Insomnia">insomnia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tooth_decay">Tooth decay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tooth decay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2003 WHO report stated that "Sugars are undoubtedly the most important dietary factor in the development of <a href="/wiki/Dental_caries" class="mw-redirect" title="Dental caries">dental caries</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-WHO2003_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2003-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> A review of human studies showed that the incidence of caries is lower when sugar intake is less than 10% of total energy consumed.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nutritional_displacement">Nutritional displacement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Nutritional displacement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Empty_calorie" class="mw-redirect" title="Empty calorie">"empty calories"</a> argument states that a diet high in added sugar will reduce consumption of foods that contain <a href="/wiki/Essential_nutrient" class="mw-redirect" title="Essential nutrient">essential nutrients</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> This nutrient displacement occurs if sugar makes up more than 25% of daily energy intake,<sup id="cite_ref-dietary_reference_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dietary_reference-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> a proportion associated with poor diet quality and risk of obesity.<sup id="cite_ref-2015_WHO_guidelines_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_WHO_guidelines-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Displacement may occur at lower levels of consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-dietary_reference_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dietary_reference-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Alzheimer.27s_disease"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Alzheimer's_disease">Alzheimer's disease</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Alzheimer&#039;s disease">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Claims have been made of a sugar–<a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer&#39;s disease">Alzheimer's disease</a> connection, but there is inconclusive evidence that cognitive decline is related to dietary fructose or overall energy intake.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recommended_dietary_intake">Recommended dietary intake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Recommended dietary intake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> recommends that both adults and children reduce the intake of free sugars to less than 10% of total energy intake, and suggests a reduction to below 5%. "Free sugars" include <a href="/wiki/Monosaccharide" title="Monosaccharide">monosaccharides</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disaccharide" title="Disaccharide">disaccharides</a> added to foods, and sugars found in fruit juice and concentrates, as well as in honey and syrups. According to the WHO, "[t]hese recommendations were based on the totality of available evidence reviewed regarding the relationship between free sugars intake and body weight (low and moderate quality evidence) and dental caries (very low and moderate quality evidence)."<sup id="cite_ref-WHO_2015p4_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_2015p4-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 20, 2016, the U.S. Food and Drug Administration announced changes to the Nutrition Facts panel displayed on all foods, to be effective by July 2018. New to the panel is a requirement to list "Added sugars" by weight and as a percent of Daily Value (DV). For vitamins and minerals, the intent of DVs is to indicate how much should be consumed. For added sugars, the guidance is that 100% DV should not be exceeded. 100% DV is defined as 50 grams. For a person consuming 2000 calories a day, 50 grams is equal to 200 calories and thus 10% of total calories—the same guidance as the World Health Organization.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> To put this in context, most 12 ounce (335 mL) cans of soda contain 39 grams of sugar. In the United States, a government survey on food consumption in 2013–2014 reported that, for men and women aged 20 and older, the average total sugar intakes—naturally occurring in foods and added—were, respectively, 125 and 99 g/day.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Measurements">Measurements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Measurements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Various culinary sugars have different densities due to differences in particle size and inclusion of moisture.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Domino_Sugar" class="mw-redirect" title="Domino Sugar">Domino Sugar</a> gives the following weight to volume conversions (in <a href="/wiki/United_States_customary_units" title="United States customary units">United States customary units</a>):<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Firmly packed brown sugar 1&#160;lb = 2.5 cups (or 1.3 L per kg, 0.77&#160;kg/L)</li>
<li>Granulated sugar 1&#160;lb = 2.25 cups (or 1.17 L per kg, 0.85&#160;kg/L)</li>
<li>Unsifted confectioner's sugar 1&#160;lb = 3.75 cups (or 2.0 L per kg, 0.5&#160;kg/L)</li></ul>
<p>The "Engineering Resources – Bulk Density Chart" published in <i>Powder and Bulk</i> gives different values for the bulk densities:<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Beet sugar 0.80 g/mL</li>
<li>Dextrose sugar 0.62 g/mL ( = 620&#160;kg/m^3)</li>
<li>Granulated sugar 0.70 g/mL</li>
<li>Powdered sugar 0.56 g/mL</li></ul>
<p><span id="History"></span>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Manufacturers of sugary products, such as <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drinks</a> and candy, and the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Association" title="Sugar Association">Sugar Research Foundation</a> have been accused of trying to influence consumers and medical associations in the 1960s and 1970s by creating doubt about the potential health hazards of sucrose overconsumption, while promoting <a href="/wiki/Saturated_fat" title="Saturated fat">saturated fat</a> as the main dietary risk factor in <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular diseases</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jama2016_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jama2016-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the criticism led to recommendations that diet <a href="/wiki/Policymaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Policymaker">policymakers</a> emphasize the need for high-quality research that accounts for multiple <a href="/wiki/Biomarker" title="Biomarker">biomarkers</a> on development of cardiovascular diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-jama2016_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jama2016-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
